     Title: IST OFC 9
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: In May 2014, DHS announced the adoption of the following updated
           preparedness standards: ASIS International SPC.1-2009,
           Organizational Resilience: Security, Preparedness and Continuity
           Management Systems – Requirements with Guidance for Use
           Standards, ISO 22301:2012: Societal security -- Business
           continuity management systems, and NFPA 1600: Disaster/Emergency
           Management and Business Continuity Programs, 2013 edition . More
           information about these standards is available through the FEMA
           Website, at http://www.fema.gov/about-ps-preptm .

[10] ID: eee6e723-97ff-4e4e-a898-8c0f7679ef69
     Title: IST OFC 1
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Establish an MOU/MOA with the agency to define the assistance
           and special services the agency will provide in the event of a
           threat, attack, or incident. An MOU/MOA can address items such
           as points of contact, notification procedures, exchange of
           threat information, access to the facility, hazards present on
           the facility, and participation in regular consults, drills, and
           exercises.

[16] ID: e5cde5c0-c265-49e0-b647-e0eb991dfff1
     Title: IST OFC 1
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Install permanent storm shutters to protect windows to help
           prevent glass breakage and stop windborne objects from
           penetrating the facility. Always use permanent storm shutters in
           areas where there will be little advance warning of high winds,
           as permanent shutters can be closed quickly, unlike temporary
           plywood covers that must be retrieved from storage and mounted
           with bolts or screws. Consult the FEMA flyer Protect Windows and
           Doors with Covers , available at http://www.fema.gov/media-
           library-data/20130726-1627-20490-
           8875/how2017_how2029_protect_windows_doors_4_11.pdf , for more
           information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[20] ID: 245e4d3d-ac2e-4c82-88c7-cfc6a70b33ea
     Title: IST OFC 5
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Explore flood-proofing retrofits such as dry floodproofing
           (i.e., measures resulting in watertight, flood-resistant
           structures), wet flood-proofing (i.e., the use of flood-damage-
           resistant materials and construction techniques to minimize
           flood damage), floodwalls, and levees. Consult Floodproofing
           Non-Residential Buildings (FEMA P-936) , available at
           http://www.fema.gov/media-library-
           data/9a50c534fc5895799321dcdd4b6083e7/P-936_8-20-13_508r.pdf ,
           for more information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[23] ID: ddadba00-6f7f-472a-afad-74da1233bb33
     Title: IST OFC 7
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Protect the facility's backup power generator and its fuel tank,
           as well as electrical and fuel supply lines, from destructive
           natural hazards. In flood hazard areas, mount the generator and
           tank securely on concrete platforms, above the expected flood
           level. If possible, move the generator and tank inside or next
           to a building or protective structure to shield them from severe
           weather events such as wind. Consult the FEMA flyer Install a
           Generator for Emergency Power , available at
           http://www.fema.gov/media-library-
           data/20130726-1627-20490-0643/how2022_generator_04_11_r1.pdf ,
           for more information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

     Text: Explore the feasibility of procuring a backup power generator to

           data/20130726-1627-20490-0643/how2022_generator_04_11_r1.pdf ,

     Title: IST OFC 10

     Text: Explore the feasibility of using natural gas to fuel the backup
           power system. While diesel, which is traditionally used to fuel
           backup power systems, is relatively safe to store onsite and
           economical to procure, re-supply for an extended period may be
           an issue. Because most natural gas infrastructure is
           underground, the natural gas supply may not be impacted by
           severe weather events. Source 1,

[29] ID: 2b8cb440-3754-4c90-84e2-5abe070b6b12
     Title: IST OFC 13
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop shelter-in-place plans for facility occupants if it is
           not safe to evacuate the facility during a natural disaster.
           Train employees on the plan, and conduct recurring exercises on,
           reviews of, and updates to the plan. Ensure contractors and
           frequent visitors to the facility are aware of these plans.
           Consult the Ready.gov Website, available at
           http://www.ready.gov/shelter , for more information on
           sheltering.

[34] ID: 323177f1-6173-4285-8613-432dc3088d19
     Title: IST OFC 18
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: If the facility does not have a backup generator, explore
           options to enter into a contract to have one readily available,
           in the event that a natural hazard disrupts power to the
           facility and its critical assets. Ensure that the facility is
           equipped (i.e., has the necessary wiring and transfer switches)
           to facilitate the rapid installation and operation of the
           generator unit.

[42] ID: 97f6a468-9ca1-4c95-8245-c16eafa79183
     Title: IST OFC 26
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Explore the feasibility of modifying or retrofitting the
           facility to make it safer during earthquakes and more resistant
           to earthquake damage and disruption. The optimal combination
           earthquake risk-reduction measures for a facility will depend on
           factors such as the potential severity of the earthquake hazards
           in the area, the current condition of the facility, whether the
           facility is owned or leased, and how vulnerable facility
           operations are to facility damage and associated downtime.
           Consult QuakeSmart, at http://www.fema.gov/quakesmart, for
           information about how to assess facility risks and how to
           develop and implement a plan to cost-effectively mitigate those
           risks.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[43] ID: 458d67d8-349c-43dc-9404-23b3c547937a
     Title: IST OFC 27
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: If the facility has cripple walls, brace the walls by adding
           2-inch by 4-inch boards between vertical studs at the top and
           bottom of the walls and, if necessary, at other locations
           between the studs. Consult the FEMA flyer Brace Cripple Walls ,
           available at http://www.fema.gov/media-library-
           data/20130726-1627-20490-0271/how2012_brace_cripple_walls.pdf ,
           for more information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

     Title: IST OFC 28
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Anchor any sill plates. Sill plates rest directly on top of a
           foundation, and bolting the plates directly into the foundation
           provides extra stability. Consult the FEMA flyer Bolt Sill
           Plates to Foundation , available at http://www.fema.gov/media-
           library-data/20130726-1627-20490-5339/how2013_sill_plates.pdf ,
           for more information.

[47] ID: 0c4db8ee-a39d-4f53-afa7-51d0cedfd025
     Title: IST OFC 32
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Establish earthquake emergency plans and procedures. Emphasize
           safe places for building occupants to "drop, cover, and hold on"
           during earthquake shaking. Establish safe locations where people
           can rendezvous when the shaking has stopped and it is safe and
           advisable to evacuate the facility. Contact the State/local
           emergency management office and/or the regional FEMA office for
           available earthquake planning resources.

[53] ID: 883c3375-077a-4336-a1ee-f8fb08407d0f
     Title: IST OFC 37
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Explore the feasibility of establishing a safe room or rooms
           specifically designed to meet FEMA criteria and provide "near-
           absolute protection" during tornadoes. To be considered a FEMA
           safe room, the structure must be designed and constructed to the
           guidelines specified in FEMA P-320, Taking Shelter from the
           Storm: Building a Safe Room for Your Home or Small Business
           (available at http://www.fema.gov/media-library-
           data/20130726-1454-20490-8914/fema_p_320.pdf ), and FEMA P-361,
           Design and Construction Guidance for Community Safe Rooms
           (available at http://www.fema.gov/media-library-
           data/20130726-1508-20490-8283/fema_p_361.pdf ). Consult the FEMA
           Webpage "Safe Rooms," at http://www.fema.gov/safe-rooms , for
           more information and additional resources.

     Title: IST OFC 2
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive security plan specific to the facility.
           Train personnel on the plan, and exercise the plan at least once
           a year. Consult The Critical Success Factor Method: Establishing

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[204] ID: b2d2b040-63d3-4b0e-a020-6ee87f43c8b4
     Title: IST OFC 3
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive security plan specific to the facility.
           The plan should address issues such as the following: protection
           of employees, contractors/vendors, visitors, and executives;
           protection of sensitive information; protection of funds;
           facility access control procedures; suspicious activity
           reporting procedures; employee termination procedures; parking;
           mail security; background checks; prohibited items; security
           force; end-of-day security checks; control and accountability of
           equipment (including keys); electronic security systems
           (including CCTV); physical security inspection programs; and
           employee security awareness training programs. Train personnel
           on the plan, and exercise the plan at least once a year.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[205] ID: 76e69a3e-de00-4e94-9b32-9d801c3e4be0
     Title: IST OFC 4
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive security plan specific to the facility.
           The plan should address topics such as the following: physical
           security measures and systems, security force, access control
           procedures, information protection, and security awareness
           training. In addition, the plan should include elements such as
           the following: an assessment of possible security risks; a
           review of threats to the facility and the facility's
           vulnerabilities; an up-to-date point of contact roster for key
           personnel responsible for security and first responders; and
           identification of critical assets or areas. Train personnel on
           the plan, and exercise the plan at least once a year.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[370] ID: 15b9e262-d135-402d-aa22-0da6f70acd1e
     Title: IST OFC 3
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive business continuity plan to be
           implemented in the aftermath of an incident. Train personnel on
           the plan, and exercise the plan at least once a year. For more

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[371] ID: 13c37a84-1955-4112-9c0d-d9543eb68fdc
     Title: IST OFC 4
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive business continuity plan to be
           implemented in the aftermath of an incident. The business
           continuity plan should contain the following elements: a)
           defined roles and responsibilities for personnel with authority
           during and following an incident; b) a process for activating
           the response; c) details to manage the immediate consequences of
           a disruptive incident (with regard to the welfare of
           individuals; strategic, tactical, and operational response
           options, and prevention of further loss or unavailability of
           prioritized activities); d) details on how and under what
           circumstances the facility will communicate with employees and
           their relatives, key interested parties, and emergency contacts;
           e) how the facility will continue or recover its prioritized
           activities within predetermined timeframes; f) details of the
           facility's media response following an incident; and g) a
           process for standing down once the incident is over. Train
           personnel on the plan, and exercise the plan at least once a
           year. For more information, visit the Ready.gov Website at
           http://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/continuity .

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[372] ID: cc56e546-e017-477e-8f4c-aa42b783ca88
     Title: IST OFC 5
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive business continuity plan to be
           implemented in the aftermath of an incident. The business
           continuity plan should identify stakeholders that need to be
           notified; critical and time-sensitive applications; alternative
           work sites; vital records, contact lists, processes, and
           functions that must be maintained; and personnel, procedures,
           and resources that are necessary while the facility recovers.
           Train personnel on the plan, and exercise the plan at least once
           a year. For more information, visit the Ready.gov Website at
           http://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/continuity .

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[373] ID: a41a6ec7-247a-49a3-be16-db9baa4584fe
     Title: IST OFC 6
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: For government agencies, a continuity of operations plan may be
           preferred to a business continuity plan. Develop a continuity of
           operations plan to document the overarching strategy, policies,
           and procedures required to support the organization's continuity
           of operations program. Visit the FEMA Website for related
           resources, at http://www.fema.gov/planning-templates .

     Title: IST OFC 7
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Refer to the Business Continuity Planning Suite, developed by
           DHS’ National Protection and Programs Directorate and FEMA, for
           assistance with business continuity planning. This tool is
           scalable for use by organizations of any size and consists of a
           business continuity plan training; automated business continuity
           plan and disaster recovery plan generators; and a self-directed
           exercise for testing an implemented business continuity plan.
           The Business Continuity Planning Suite is available at
           http://www.ready.gov/business-continuity-planning-suite .

[377] ID: bee63001-5300-44f7-8cae-7abf89dbf44f
     Title: IST OFC 10
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Acquire the signature and approval of a senior manager or
           designated representative for the business continuity plan. The
           successful establishment of business continuity management is
           dependent upon its integration with strategic and day-to-day
           facility management and its alignment with business priorities.
           To be effective, business continuity management must be
           recognized from the outset by senior management. Business
           continuity management must always start at the top – for the
           essential reason that business continuity management is about
           what’s important and time-sensitive. Source 1,

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[387] ID: af4fe5c1-2542-4479-90e5-4f3fe88ad8a6
     Title: IST OFC 20
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Evaluate the business continuity plan through annual exercises.
           Ensure exercises are designed to accomplish the following: 1)
           Identify planning and procedural deficiencies; 2) Test or
           validate recently changed procedures or plans; 3) Clarify roles
           and responsibilities; 4) Obtain participant feedback and
           recommendations for program improvement; 5) Measure improvement
           compared to performance objectives; 6) Improve coordination
           between internal and external teams, organizations, and
           entities; 7) Validate training and education; and 8) Identify
           additional resources and assess the capabilities of existing
           resources, including personnel and equipment needed for
           effective business continuity and recovery.

[453] ID: 961f0930-87b3-472e-9a0c-d5c535214eea
     Title: IST OFC 91
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop a comprehensive emergency operation/emergency action
           plan specific to the facility. The emergency operation/action
           plan should assign responsibilities for carrying out specific
           actions to protect people (including those with special needs),
           property, operations, and the environment in an emergency, and
           to provide incident stabilization. Train personnel on the plan,
           and exercise the plan at least once a year. For more
           information, visit the Ready.gov Website at
           http://www.ready.gov/business/implementation/emergency , and
           consult Developing and Maintaining Emergency Operations Plans ,
           available at
           http://www.fema.gov/pdf/about/divisions/npd/CPG_101_V2.pdf .

[471] ID: 8873cfb7-ed6c-4656-85d0-9d43c93a3f4c
     Title: IST OFC 109
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Evaluate the emergency operation/emergency action plan through
           annual exercises. Ensure exercises are designed to accomplish
           the following: 1) Identify planning and procedural deficiencies;
           2) Test or validate recently changed procedures or plans; 3)
           Clarify roles and responsibilities; 4) Obtain participant
           feedback and recommendations for program improvement; 5) Measure
           improvement compared to performance objectives; 6) Improve
           coordination between internal and external teams, organizations,
           and entities; 7) Validate training and education; 8) Increase
           awareness and understanding of hazards and the potential impacts
           of hazards on the facility; and 9) Identify additional resources
           and assess the capabilities of existing resources, including
           personnel and equipment needed for effective response.

[578] ID: 3cbe8837-7d64-411a-b0f6-fbe0f260c6cb
     Title: IST OFC 46
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Develop post orders that describe in detail the duties and
           responsibilities of the security force. After comprehensive post
           orders are developed, ensure that they are kept current and
           accessible. Comprehensive post orders may serve to express the
           policies of the protected enterprise, summarize required officer
           duties, avoid problems associated with of word-of-mouth
           instructions, and provide a basis for site-specific training.
           They are the vital link between the requirements of the facility
           and the ability of security personnel to effectively meet those
           requirements.

[581] ID: 2127d2b3-ce1c-4221-97dc-85455cf53373
     Title: IST OFC 2
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Consider the installation of fencing with the following
           attributes: Type - chain link OR - anti-climb aluminum or steel
           chain link OR - standard aluminum or steel chain link OR -
           concrete OR - brick and mortar OR - steel OR - wrought iron
           Height - 7 ft. high OR - 8 ft. high OR - 9 ft. high Base of
           Fence - anchored base Outriggers - outriggers OR - outriggers
           angled at 45 degrees OR - outriggers in a "Y"/"V" configuration
           Enhancements - K-rated for vehicle penetration - cabling to
           provide additional crash resistance - coiled razor wire along
           the top of the fence - coiled barbed wire along the top of the
           fence - coiled razor wire along the bottom of the fence - coiled
           barbed wire along the bottom of the fence - spikes along the top
           to prevent scaling - privacy screening

     Text: Anchor the base of the fence to protect against access by
           crawling under or raising lower portion of fence. The fence
           should also be installed to preclude access made possible by
           ground erosion.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[602] ID: d5d7ce29-2596-46f2-95e5-f247a2a4bf29
     Title: IST OFC 20
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Extend the fencing fabric to within 2 inches of firm ground, and
           anchor the base of the fence using horizontal bottom rails,
           tension wires, concrete curbs, sills, sheet piling, piping, or
           other inexpensive materials. Horizontal bottom rails, concrete
           curbs, or sills can mitigate the ability to lift the fence
           fabric by hand (e.g., no more than 5 inches).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[603] ID: 70b79896-541e-4b55-bed4-d4ee8b4c279d
     Title: IST OFC 21
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Bury the fence fabric (e.g., 12 inches into the ground) for
           additional security. This may also prevent the fencing fabric
           from being lifted (for example, by more than 5 inches). However,
           corrosion of the buried fabric must be monitored.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[604] ID: 336d3742-4d4b-4654-8ba8-ee2b63c90926
     Title: IST OFC 22
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Equip the fence with outriggers that are angled out and away
           from the facility to make climbing the fence more difficult and
           to prevent ladders from being placed against it. The overhang
           should extend far enough to increase the height of the fence by
           at least 1 foot. Consult UFC 4-022-03, Security Fences and Gates
           , available at http://www.wbdg.org/ccb/DOD/UFC/ufc_4_022_03.pdf
           , and Access Control Point Standard Drawings and Criteria ,
           available at https://pdc.usace.army.mil/library/drawings/acp ,
           for more information. Source 1,

[605] ID: 96d793c5-121f-4be0-aa56-b3e2270f2b97
     Title: IST OFC 23
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Install outriggers with connecting wire, such as three strands
           of barbed wire at regular intervals, along the top of the fence.
           Outriggers typically face outward (i.e., away from the facility)
           and upward at approximately a 45-degree angle.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[606] ID: 6074827c-aede-4f67-8ed6-f321de2576a5
     Title: IST OFC 24
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Install outriggers (support arms) at 45-degree angles in a
           single arm (towards the threat side) or “Y”/”V” configuration,
           constructed of a single or double outrigger consisting of
           18-inch (457 mm) arm(s), each having three strands of barbed
           wire at regular intervals along the top of the fence. The
           outriggers should provide a minimum of an additional 12 inches
           to the fence height. Consult Access Control Point Standard
           Drawings and Criteria , available at
           https://pdc.usace.army.mil/library/drawings/acp , for more
           information.

[615] ID: 92459947-71e4-4f17-9965-e45d735a2463
     Title: IST OFC 33
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Explore the feasibility of installing "tangle-foot wire."
           Tangle-foot wire is barbed wire strung across two posts no
           higher than 12 inches. It is used outside a perimeter fence or
           between double fences to provide extra protection from an
           intruder. Liability issues should be considered when installing
           tangle-foot wire.

     Text: Establish clear zones on both sides of the fence to provide an

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[618] ID: 35b2b9dc-5dd0-4fe8-b96a-b480a9990241
     Title: IST OFC 36
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Ensure clear zones are free of debris, vegetation, and any items
           that could provide cover and concealment. When it is impossible
           to have adequate clear zones because of property lines or
           natural or manmade features, it may be necessary to increase the
           height of the perimeter barrier, increase security-patrol
           coverage, and/or add more security lighting along that portion
           of the perimeter. Failure to establish and maintain a clear zone
           along the fence minimizes its effectiveness. Consult Site and
           Urban Design for Security: Guidance against Potential Terrorist
           Attacks (FEMA 430), available at http://www.fema.gov/media-
           library-data/20130726-1624-20490-9648/fema430.pdf, for more
           information. Source 1 , Source 2,

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[619] ID: df1f2f75-1199-489c-9ab8-b7a03b0ed3dd
     Title: IST OFC 37
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Ensure that for high security applications a clear zone of 20
           feet or more separates a perimeter barrier from exterior
           structures, parking areas, and natural features. A clear zone of
           50 feet or more should separate a perimeter barrier from
           structures within the protected area, except when a building
           wall constitutes part of a perimeter barrier.Consult Site and
           Urban Design for Security: Guidance against Potential Terrorist
           Attacks (FEMA 430), available at http://www.fema.gov/media-
           library-data/20130726-1624-20490-9648/fema430.pdf, for more
           information.

           through a remote area.

[689] ID: dcf68176-484a-4c45-8bb3-e541c22f7ba8
     Title: IST OFC 6
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: (1) Determine the facility’s susceptibility to blast. Consult
           Reference Manual to Mitigate Potential Terrorist Attacks Against
           Buildings (FEMA 426/BIPS 06) , available at
           http://www.dhs.gov/xlibrary/assets/st/st-bips-06.pdf , for more
           information, especially Chapters 2 and 3: Chapter 2 discusses
           blast design concerns and protective measures for areas
           surrounding buildings. Chapter 3 discusses the nature of
           explosive blasts, their effects on buildings and occupants, and
           the concept of levels of protection. In addition, review the DHS
           Bomb Threat Stand-off Chart , available through the Lessons
           Learned Information Sharing national, online network, at
           https://www.llis.dhs.gov/sites/default/files/DHS-
           BombThreatChart-6-5-09.pdf . (2) Based on the facility’s
           potential vulnerabilities, explore the feasibility of conducting
           a preliminary blast analysis using simple, commercially
           available building modeling and software designed to support the
           ability to address blast mitigation and potential VBIED threats,
           such as A.T.-BLAST by ARA Applied Research Associates. (3) Based
           on the results from the preliminary blast analysis, explore the
           feasibility of consulting with an engineering firm that
           specializes in structural fragility to procure a professional
           blast assessment to inform capital investments intended to
           protect personnel and the facility against blast.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

     Text: Install a bollard system that is well-integrated into the
           perimeter security design and the streetscape to minimize visual
           impact. Bollard height should typically not be more than 30
           inches. Bollard spacing should be between 36 and 43 inches,
           depending on the kind of traffic expected and the needs of
           pedestrians and the handicapped.

           heavy objects and trees, walls and ha-ha barriers, water
           obstacles, and Jersey barriers.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Install fixed bollards, engineered planters, and/or heavy
           objects, such as boulders and sculptures, to increase standoff
           distance from a potential explosive device and reduce damage.

           laminated glass).

[741] ID: c441c8ca-b84a-40e5-92b7-6589cc6ef559
     Title: IST OFC 2
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Apply anti-shatter film to existing glass to provide fragment
           retention and reduce the overall velocity of glass fragments at
           failure, especially near regularly occupied and mass-gathering
           areas. Anti-shatter film may mitigate the impact of wind-blown
           debris and seismic stress in addition to explosive force by
           preventing pieces of broken glass from becoming lethal
           projectiles.

[772] ID: 3d6806c1-b31c-4932-a697-14821cf49c7e
     Title: IST OFC 2
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Evaluate the weakest areas of the exterior and install IDS
           sensors as appropriate. The basic types of sensors used for
           exterior intrusion are buried-line sensors, fence-associated
           sensors, and freestanding sensors. The IDS should be evenly
           distributed throughout critical areas to ensure uniform
           detection around the entire length of the facility’s perimeter.
           Sensors should be placed in locations that avoid
           electromagnetic, acoustic, thermal, nuclear radiation, optical,
           seismic, and meteorological interferences.

[788] ID: f6314082-be1b-407b-bb02-25beae6220e5
     Title: IST OFC 18
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Explore the feasibility of installing a comprehensive CCTV
           system onsite. Site-specific factors must be considered when
           selecting components that comprise a particular CCTV system. For
           example, the size of the system, in terms of the number of
           cameras needed, is the minimum number required to view all
           electronic security system sensor detection fields. In addition,
           some cameras may require artificial light sources. Finally,
           performance criteria and physical, environmental, and economic
           considerations must be factored into the component selection.

[813] ID: 4c2ad56a-4976-46e5-9b62-47f739df6694
     Title: IST OFC 5
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Providing a minimum surface lighting average of 4 horizontal
           foot-candles at gates to help ensure adequate lighting for
           pedestrians, islands, and guards in approach and exit zones.
           However, this level is inadequate in entry control zones where
           IDs will be checked. Guardhouse and ID check positions should
           have a minimum of 10 foot-candles, with 20 foot-candles
           preferred. (A foot-candle is a unit of illuminance on a surface
           that is everywhere 1 foot from a uniform point source of light
           of one candle and equal to 1 lumen per square foot. To convert
           foot-candles to watts, first convert foot-candles into lumens,
           then convert lumens into watts. One foot-candle equals 10.76
           lumens, and 1 lumen equals 0.001496 watts.) Source 1,

[857] ID: abe41c2a-b450-41ed-81ea-2b756d8226d7
     Title: IST OFC 20
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Conduct an assessment to determine which systems and equipment
           are essential to the continued operation of the facility. They
           may include one or more of the following: HVAC systems;
           industrial equipment and major appliances; lights (interior and
           exterior), computers, and other office equipment; pumps,
           including sump pumps, sprinkler system pumps, and well water
           pumps; and alarm systems. Once essential systems and equipment
           have been identified, determine how much power they require, and
           then consult with a generator technical expert regarding the
           appropriate size and type of generator(s) for the facility. The
           technical expert can also help select other components of the
           emergency power system, including the main transfer switch and
           the electrical panel.

[915] ID: 4fb7bfcb-6a3a-4e97-b832-79578fb228a3
     Title: IST OFC 3
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Report all cyber incidents to appropriate outside organizations.
           Cyber incident reports can be made to request technical
           assistance, request incident management support, and/or for
           information sharing. Information sharing plays a key role in the
           prevention of cyber attacks and ensures new threats can be
           identified quickly and effective countermeasures can be
           developed to neutralize/defeat them. Cyber threats/attack
           techniques are continuously evolving and change on a daily
           basis; many organizations/companies may be unaware of these
           latest threats. Participating in information sharing with other
           outside organizations and facilities may reduce this
           vulnerability and could possibly prevent a future cybersecurity
           attack from being successful.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[916] ID: a24e663b-c730-4246-9b2c-c44540cd9d23
     Title: IST OFC 4
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Ensure facility IT representatives actively participate in
           cybersecurity forums. Examples of such forums include sector-
           specific information sharing and analysis centers, sector-
           related associations/partnerships, Federal or State-led
           partnerships (e.g., FBI InfraGard chapters), fusion centers,
           State or local law enforcement departments, and State or local
           IT offices.

           removed using proper sanitation methods, or media destruction,
           to ensure information is not released during disposal of
           protected assets. Consult NIST SP 800-53 Revision 4: Security
           and Privacy Controls for Federal Information Systems and
           Organizations , available here , for more information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[939] ID: 6107e73c-2d21-4c28-b482-02579345219b
     Title: IST OFC 27
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Incident response/management: This element captures the means of
           the facility to detect and respond to five categories of cyber
           incidents: Unauthorized Access, DOS, Malicious Code, Improper
           Usage, and Scans/Probes/Attempted Access. The incidents listed
           can be detected by multiple technical means including intrusion
           detection/prevention systems, firewalls, anti-virus tools, and
           vulnerability detection/assessment tools. Managing responses to
           incidents is necessary to ensure that incidents are properly
           detected and reported so that the incident is handled properly,
           forensic evidence is not lost, and essential operations are
           recovered as soon as possible.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[940] ID: 49917269-76d5-4575-a751-71a284843f99
     Title: IST OFC 28
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Unauthorized access, i.e., an individual gains logical or
           physical access without permission to a network, system,
           application, data, or other resource. Unauthorized access may
           result in release of sensitive information or disruption of
           business operations.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[941] ID: 075da779-6c87-447f-875c-69573748d8cb
     Title: IST OFC 29
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: DOS, i.e., an attack that successfully prevents or impairs the
           normal authorized functionality of networks, systems, or
           applications by exhausting resources. This activity includes
           being the victim or participating in the DOS. Defending against
           DOS attacks can benefit from detecting the presence of an attack
           and receiving external support to block incoming network
           traffic.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[942] ID: 9a5af60b-6175-4ed7-ab53-d3d2578e85fc
     Title: IST OFC 30
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Malicious code, i.e., the successful installation of malicious
           software (e.g., virus, worm, Trojan horse, or other code-based
           malicious entity) that infects an operating system or
           application.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[943] ID: d9d90cac-923e-4b86-aa72-a585d0dba303
     Title: IST OFC 31
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Improper usage, i.e., a person violates acceptable computing use
           policies. Improper usage can result in the leak of sensitive
           information, the introduction of malicious code, the loss of
           system or information integrity, or other security-related
           events.

[944] ID: c262abf6-6e3f-4245-88bd-0080a411a10c
     Title: IST OFC 27
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Scan/probes/attempted access, i.e., any activity that seeks to
           access or identify a computer, open parts, protocols, service,
           or any combination for later exploit. Use intrusion detection
           and prevention software or network behavior analysis software to
           detect anomalous external network traffic, such as scanning.
           Participate in regional information sharing to receive
           information about active scanning or network-based security
           attacks.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[945] ID: bc9e512a-33ae-492c-88b6-27bb620e4e17
     Title: IST OFC 33
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Security testing: Testing is necessary to verify and validate
           that the intended security rules are properly implemented.
           Vulnerabilities include software holes that a hacker might take
           advantage of, out of date virus definition files, default
           passwords set by a vendor, or accounts that are not password
           protected. Software designed for scanning, such as ISS or
           Nessus, is commonly used, as is active scan systems, which
           detect vulnerabilities as soon as a system joins the network.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[946] ID: 31220758-92c4-42cc-bd5b-db2548f2d489
     Title: IST OFC 35
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Firewalls: Firewalls are devices or programs that control the
           flow of network traffic between networks or hosts that employ
           differing security postures. Without a firewall, internal
           systems are exposed to potential attacks against which they
           might not have sufficient protection. Consult NIST SP 800-41:
           Guidelines on Firewalls and Firewall Policy , available here ,
           for more information.

[948] ID: fb34b51f-1301-4ced-b078-56cb6c297890
     Title: IST OFC 37
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Remote access: Remote access introduces numerous vulnerabilities
           ranging from lack of physical security on remote access devices
           (home computers, phones, tables), potential malware on those
           remote devices, information travels over unsecured networks
           (Internet), and opening internal resources to external devices.
           Securing remote access requires encrypting traffic from the
           remote devices, using technologies such as VPN, and strictly
           enforcing authentication. Consult NIST SP 800-46: Guide to
           Enterprise Telework and Remote Access Security , available here
           , for more information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[949] ID: 8e3f1bcb-d3bf-41e0-b61c-9263ca269b23
     Title: IST OFC 38
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Wireless connectivity: Wireless technologies are typically less
           secure than wired technologies, primarily because they can
           extend outside of the physical footprint of the organization,
           but also because they often have weak security configurations. A
           best-case scenario would be for wireless to not be used at all,
           especially on control networks. Other scenarios may have a
           separate visitor network space, such that a visitor would not be
           able to scan traffic on the internal network. Employees would
           need to VPN or authenticate in some manner to gain access. A
           worst-case scenario would be that wireless is open to all, and
           exists on the same network as the internal systems. Consult NIST
           SP 800-153: Guidelines for Securing Wireless Local Area Networks
           (WLANs) , available here , for more information on securing
           wireless technology.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[950] ID: cde5c60a-db50-437b-b5bc-0e3c0c18241a
     Title: IST OFC 39
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Security patches or updates: A "patch" is a piece of computer
           code that a software company writes and distributes to fix a
           problem found in one of its previously released programs. Many
           patches fix problems related to security—specifically,
           vulnerabilities in the programs that attackers can exploit.
           Hackers seek out these vulnerabilities to gain access to a
           computer and its information, which then can be used to gain
           access to other vulnerable computers and information. These
           compromised computers also can be used to attack other
           computers. To prevent these problems, patches need to be
           deployed to computer systems quickly to minimize the window of
           opportunity for attackers. Consult NIST SP 800-40 Revision 3:
           Guide to Enterprise Patch Management Technologies , available
           here , for more information.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[951] ID: 66b54303-2474-40b0-b1d8-b7af5c7b9929
     Title: IST OFC 40
     Created: 2026-01-21 20:40:15.279932+00:00
     Text: Conduct regular cybersecurity exercises. An exercise is a
           simulation of an emergency designed to validate the viability of
           one or more aspects of an IT plan. In an exercise, personnel
           with roles and responsibilities in a particular IT plan meet to
           validate the content of a plan through discussion of their roles
           and their responses to emergency situations, execution of
           responses in a simulated operational environment, or other means
           of validating responses that does not involve using the actual
           operational environment. Exercises are scenario-driven, such as
           a power failure in one of the organization’s data centers or a
           fire causing certain systems to be damaged, with additional
           situations often being presented during the course of an
           exercise.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

           achieved, the effectiveness of participation, and the adequacy
           of cybersecurity response policies and procedures in the event
           of a real cybersecurity attack. Modify cybersecurity plans,
           policies, and procedures as necessary.

     Text: Implement LAN segmentation physically or with VLANs. Use routing
           to provide systems cross-connectivity only where necessary.
           Employ access control measures to restrict access between
           segmented networks. Managed interfaces include, for example,
           gateways, routers, firewalls, guards, network-based malicious
           code analysis and virtualization systems, and encrypted tunnels
           implemented within a security architecture (e.g., routers
           protecting firewalls or application gateways residing on
           protected subnetworks). Restricting or prohibiting interfaces
           within organizational information systems includes, for example,
           restricting external Web traffic to designated Web servers
           within managed interfaces and prohibiting external traffic that
           appears to be spoofing internal addresses. Consider the shared
           nature of commercial telecommunications services in the
           implementation of security controls associated with the use of
           such services. Commercial telecommunications services are
           commonly based on network components and consolidated management
           systems shared by all attached commercial customers, and may
           also include third party-provided access lines and other service
           elements. Such transmission services may represent sources of
           increased risk despite contract security provisions. Source 1,
           Source 2,

           rapid restoration of deliveries. Establish a liaison with the
           provider(s) to maintain communications during a supply
           disruption. Ensure the contingency/business continuity plan is
           well understood by facility management and employees.
